Another challenge in phylogenetics is the problem of homoplasy, which occurs when two or more organisms evolve similar characteristics independently of each other. But the women of the Greenwich Equal Franchise League refused to back down. Undeterred by the jeers and catcalls, they pressed on, undaunted by the prospect of arrest and imprisonment.

For behind every placard, every banner, and every stride, beat the steady drumbeat of a long-forgotten dream - the dream of a more equal society, where a woman's right to vote was a fundamental human right, every bit as sacrosanct as a man's.

"We shall not be silenced," declared the league's fiery leader, Maria White, her voice ringing through the city's very streets. "We shall not be deterred. For we know that our struggle is the struggle of all women, everywhere, and that our victory shall be the dawn of a brighter, fairer world."

As the years drew on, the Greenwich Equal Franchise League's influence spread, touching the hearts and minds of women and men across the land. And though the road to victory was long and arduous, the league's unshakeable resolve ultimately prevailed.
